Program<br /> <br /> Patrisia Mac&amp;#237;as (SLC alumna), Sociology<br /> University of Illinois, Chicago<br /> <br /> In 2010, the Department of Homeland Security issued guidelines to target enforcement resources on &amp;#8220;national security risks&amp;#8221; and &amp;#8220;criminal offenders&amp;#8221; in order to keep deportable but low-priority immigrants from &amp;#8220;clogging the system.&amp;#8221; Despite this public commitment to deprioritize immigrants with no criminal record, deportations continue to rise. exuberant paintings, combining an <a href="https://www.artsy.net/gene/abstract-expressionism">Abstract Expressionistic</a> style with comic strip characters of her own invention. Though the recurring figure of a young girl and her animal consorts suggest narratives, Berkenblit sees these figures as collections of lines, devices that organize and drive her overall composition. As she explains: &amp;#8220;The figures I choose have one purpose: they carry the line that I wish to draw. The figures are not symbolic; they don't represent anyone or anything in particular. They are the perfect excuse to get the first line going.&amp;#8221; In <em>Tigers vs Witches</em> (2013), the profiles of a tiger and a witch face each other across the canvas. 'recurring' => True, 'title' => "Michael Dumanis—Repetition &amp; Variation: The Poetics of Obsession and Accumulation ", 'summary' => "", 'content' => "<p><p>The repetition of diction and syntax to advance one&amp;#8217;s rhetoric and build energy in a text is an ancient poetic device. One can encounter it in the <em>Book of Numbers</em> and <em>The Song of Songs</em> in the Old Testament, as well as in Homer and Hesiod&amp;#8212;and it&amp;#8217;s also a common practice in contemporary poetry. The relentless repetition of a chain of words has the power of casting a spell over a reader, of seducing, hypnotizing, and comforting. Repetition is intrinsically nostalgic, causing the reader to look back, whereas to vary from a pattern signals change and propels the poem onward. Repetition also provides the opportunity to riff and to take the same idea in a disparate number of unexpected directions in the same text, to explore a concept until its exhaustion. In this craft session we will investigate how a rhetoric of repetition serves both as an organizing principle for and as an engine driving forward a diverse number of modern and contemporary poets, including Dorothea Lasky, Lisa Jarnot, Juliana Spahr, Shane McCrae, Olena Kalytiak Davis, and Inger Christensen.</p></p>", 'page_url' => "https://www.sarahlawrence.edu/news-events/events/2015-2016/2016-04-19-michael_dumanis_craf-eid213409.html", 'share_url' => "https://www.sarahlawrence.edu/news-events/events/2015-2016/2016-04-19-michael_dumanis_craf-eid213409.html", 'ical_url' => "https://www.sarahlawrence.edu/news-events/events/event.ics?e=2016-04-19-michael_dumanis_craf-eid213409", 'location' => "Slonim Living Room", 'academics' => array( "MFA Writing" ), 'themes' => array( ), 'audiences' => array( "Public", "Graduate" ), 'sponsors' => array( ), 'faculty' => array( ) ), array( 'id' => 214081, 'start' => 1461087000000, 'end' => 1461092400000, 'all_day' => False, 'recurring' => True, 'title' => "Music Tuesday—Manhattan String Quartet", 'summary' => "", 'content' => "<p><p><span>Music Tuesday presents&amp;#160;Manhattan String Quartet;
